================================================================================
NOTE: note_049
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Procedure Note

Indication:
Benign bronchial stenosis of bronchus intermedius with recurrent post-obstructive symptoms.

Procedure:
Flexible bronchoscopy, balloon dilation, and covered metallic stent placement.

Findings:
Bronchus intermedius narrowed to approximately 3-4 mm by mixed cicatricial change and extrinsic distortion. Right upper lobe already surgically absent. Distal middle and lower lobe airways patent after intervention.

Technique:
Under general anesthesia the stenotic segment was traversed with difficulty. Balloon dilation performed serially to 10 mm. Because of elastic recoil, a short covered metallic stent was deployed in the bronchus intermedius with good expansion and preserved distal airway patency.

Specimens:
None.

Complications:
None immediate.

Plan:
Nebulized saline, secretion clearance, follow-up bronchoscopy for stent check.

<<<END NOTE>>>

STATUS: SUCCESS

================================================================================
NOTE: note_035
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Central airway obstruction from benign tracheal granulation tissue around tracheostomy site.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same, improved after intervention.

PROCEDURES PERFORMED
Rigid bronchoscopy
Mechanical debridement
Cryotherapy
Bronchoscopy through tracheostomy stoma

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia with jet ventilation.

FINDINGS
Granulation tissue arising from anterior tracheal wall near prior tracheostomy site, producing approximately 60% tracheal narrowing. Distal trachea and main bronchi patent.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
Rigid bronchoscope inserted orally. Granulation tissue removed with forceps and treated with cryotherapy. Bronchoscope then passed through the tracheostomy stoma to inspect tract and confirm no posterior wall injury. Final airway caliber significantly improved.

SPECIMENS
Granulation tissue.

COMPLICATIONS
None immediate.

PLAN
Humidification, trach care, and follow-up airway surveillance.

<<<END NOTE>>>

NOTE: note_030

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Indication:
PET-avid left upper lobe peripheral lesion.

Procedure:
Computer-assisted guided bronchoscopy using Galaxy platform, radial EBUS, fluoroscopy, fiducial placement, and TBNA/forceps biopsy.

Findings:
Target in the apicoposterior LUL was reached with guided bronchoscopy. Radial EBUS gave an eccentric signal. Fiducials were placed adjacent to the lesion after tissue sampling. No endobronchial disease.

Sampling:
TBNA x3
Forceps biopsy x5

Specimens:
LUL lesion aspirates and biopsies.

Complications:
Trace bleeding at biopsy site, controlled with wedging. No immediate pneumothorax.

Plan:
Chest x-ray post-procedure. Fiducials in expected region on fluoroscopy.

<<<END NOTE>>>

NOTE: note_007

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PREPROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Need for surveillance bronchoscopy after silicone Y stent placement.

POSTPROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Granulation tissue at proximal right limb; retained secretions cleared; stent remains in satisfactory position.

PROCEDURE
Flexible bronchoscopy with airway inspection, secretion clearance, granulation tissue cryotherapy, and stent revision not required.

INDICATION
History of malignant carinal involvement treated with silicone Y stent. Increased cough and wheeze.

FINDINGS
Silicone Y stent seated appropriately. Moderate inspissated secretions within tracheal limb and right bronchial limb. Small rim of granulation tissue at proximal right mainstem end causing mild focal narrowing. No migration. Left limb widely patent.

DESCRIPTION
Bronchoscope was introduced through the ETT. Secretions were suctioned from all stent limbs. Granulation tissue was treated with short freeze-thaw cryotherapy applications. Final inspection showed improved patency. No repositioning was necessary.

SPECIMENS
None.

COMPLICATIONS
None.

PLAN
Continue airway clearance regimen. Repeat surveillance bronchoscopy in 6-8 weeks or earlier for symptoms.

NOTE: note_040

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Pulmonary alveolar proteinosis, second-stage lavage of right lung.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same.

PROCEDURE
Bronchoscopic confirmation of double-lumen tube followed by right whole lung lavage.

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia.

FINDINGS
Double-lumen tube position satisfactory. Initial right lung return was cloudy white with particulate material, gradually clearing after serial cycles.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
Right lung isolated. Warmed saline was instilled in 500-1000 mL aliquots with chest percussion during drainage. Total instilled volume 16 liters; total return volume 14.9 liters. Effluent progressively less opaque by end of procedure. One brief episode of hypotension responded to vasopressor adjustment.

SPECIMENS
Lavage fluid sample retained.

COMPLICATIONS
Transient hypotension, resolved.

DISPOSITION
Transferred to ICU intubated for post-procedure monitoring.

NOTE: note_010

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_<<<NOTE _TAGS: extreme_length

PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Left upper lobe pulmonary nodule with mediastinal adenopathy; need for diagnosis and staging.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same, status post computer-assisted navigational bronchoscopy (Galaxy platform), radial EBUS, fluoroscopy, cone-beam CT confirmation, transbronchial sampling, BAL, and linear EBUS staging.

PROCEDURES PERFORMED

1. Flexible bronchoscopy with complete airway inspection
2. Computer-assisted navigational bronchoscopy to LUL peripheral target
3. Radial EBUS confirmation
4. Cone-beam CT spin with confirmation of tool-in-lesion
5. Transbronchial needle aspiration, forceps biopsy, transbronchial biopsy, and cryobiopsy of target lesion
6. BAL, lingula
7. Linear EBUS-TBNA of stations 4L, 7, and 11L

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia via endotracheal tube.

INDICATION
Enlarging spiculated LUL lesion with FDG-avid left hilar and mediastinal nodes.

FINDINGS
Airways were normal to the segmental level except for mild anthracotic change in the left upper lobe. The peripheral target was reached via an apicoposterior route based on pre-procedure planning. Radial EBUS gave an eccentric but reproducible signal. Cone-beam CT demonstrated the biopsy tool within the lesion after minor catheter adjustment. No endobronchial tumor identified. Nodal stations 4L and 11L were enlarged; station 7 mildly enlarged.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
After induction and timeout, flexible bronchoscopy was performed with complete airway inspection. The navigational platform was registered and advanced to the LUL target. Assisted navigation was used to align with the lesion. Radial EBUS probe was inserted through the working channel and confirmed the lesion. A cone-beam CT spin was then obtained, showing near-central tool position, after which sampling proceeded. TBNA was performed x4 passes, forceps biopsy x5, fluoroscopic transbronchial biopsy x4, and cryobiopsy x2. Minor bleeding after one cryobiopsy specimen was controlled with wedging, suction, and iced saline. BAL of the lingula was then performed with 120 mL instilled and 45 mL returned. The linear EBUS bronchoscope was introduced and systematic nodal staging performed in the sequence 11L, 4L, 7. Station 11L underwent 4 passes, station 4L 5 passes, and station 7 3 passes. ROSE was present and showed diagnostic lesional material from the peripheral target and adequate lymphoid tissue from the nodes.

SPECIMENS
LUL lesion TBNA
LUL lesion forceps biopsies
LUL lesion TBBx
LUL lesion cryobiopsies
Lingula BAL
EBUS-TBNA 11L x4
EBUS-TBNA 4L x5
EBUS-TBNA 7 x3

COMPLICATIONS
Minor endobronchial bleeding resolved during the <<<NOTE . No immediate pneumothorax or hemodynamic instability.

IMPRESSION
Successful combined diagnostic and staging bronchoscopy using navigational and EBUS modalities.

PLAN
Portable chest radiograph in PACU. Follow pathology, cytology, and microbiology. Telephone discussion of results when available.

<<<END NOTE>>>

Narrative op note

The patient underwent linear EBUS-TBNA for staging of a right hilar mass. Limited bronchoscopy showed mild extrinsic narrowing of the right upper lobe bronchus but no visible endobronchial lesion. EBUS identified abnormal lymph nodes at stations 10R, 4R, and 7. Sampling was performed in the order 10R, 7, then 4R. Pass counts were 3, 4, and 5 respectively. ROSE was present and confirmed adequacy at each station, with atypical cells favored from 10R and 4R. There were no immediate complications. Plan is recovery per protocol and await final cytology.

================================================================================
NOTE: note_015
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_<<<NOTE _TAGS: ambiguous_laterality

Procedure:
Ultrasound-guided chest tube placement for pleural infection.

Indication:
Loculated left pleural effusion with fever and pleuritic pain.

Findings:
Bedside ultrasound initially documented a right-sided pocket in error; final site confirmation and procedure were performed on the left. Complex septated pleural fluid was present.

Technique:
Patient placed sitting upright. Under sterile technique and ultrasound guidance, a 12 Fr pigtail chest tube was inserted into the left pleural space using Seldinger technique. Immediate return of thick cloudy fluid. Tube secured and connected to suction.

Specimens:
Pleural fluid sent for Gram stain, culture, pH, glucose, LDH.

Complications:
None immediate.

Plan:
Maintain suction. Consider intrapleural fibrinolytic therapy depending on drainage and imaging.

<<<END NOTE>>>

INDICATION
Whole lung lavage for pulmonary alveolar proteinosis, left lung first.

PROCEDURE
Double-lumen endotracheal tube confirmation by bronchoscopy, left whole lung lavage.

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia.

FINDINGS
Double-lumen tube position confirmed bronchoscopically with isolation of the right lung. Initial left lung effluent was opaque and milky. Progressive clearing noted with serial aliquots.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
After confirmation of tube position, the left lung was lavaged with warmed saline in sequential aliquots. Chest percussion was performed during drainage cycles. A total of 14 liters was instilled with 12.8 liters returned. Effluent transitioned from dense cloudy/milky to lighter opalescent fluid. Hemodynamics remained stable aside from brief mild hypothermia corrected with warming measures.

SPECIMENS
Representative lavage effluent sent for analysis.

COMPLICATIONS
Transient desaturation during one drainage cycle, improved with pause and ventilatory adjustment.

DISPOSITION/PLAN
Transferred intubated to ICU for continued monitoring and planned extubation when appropriate.

STATUS: SUCCESS

================================================================================
NOTE: note_011
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Severe left mainstem bronchial stenosis after prior intubation injury.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same, status post balloon dilation and electrocautery incisions.

PROCEDURES
Flexible bronchoscopy
Electrocautery radial incisions
Balloon dilation of left mainstem bronchus

FINDINGS
Short fibrotic stenosis in proximal left mainstem bronchus, approximately 4 mm residual lumen over 8-10 mm segment. Distal left-sided airways patent. No active infection or tumor.

DETAILS
Under general anesthesia, bronchoscopy showed concentric benign-appearing scar stenosis. Electrocautery knife used to create several radial incisions. Controlled balloon dilation then performed serially to 8 mm and 10 mm with improved lumen caliber. Final bronchoscopy showed approximately 9-10 mm lumen with easy passage of scope.

SPECIMENS
None.

COMPLICATIONS
None immediate.

PLAN
Observe overnight for airway symptoms. Repeat bronchoscopy as clinically indicated.

<<<END NOTE>>>

NOTE: note_002
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Left pleural effusion
POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS: Same

Procedure: Ultrasound-guided left thoracentesis

Indication:
Progressive dyspnea with recurrent unilateral pleural effusion.

Consent:
Obtained from patient after discussion of bleeding, infection, pneumothorax, and re-expansion pulmonary edema.

Technique:
Left posterior chest evaluated with ultrasound in sitting position. Moderate free-flowing anechoic effusion identified with adjacent compressed lung. Skin marked, prepped, draped. Local anesthesia with lidocaine. One-step thoracentesis catheter advanced over rib into pleural space with immediate return of clear yellow fluid.

Findings:
900 mL straw-colored fluid removed. No septations seen. Pleural pressure not formally monitored. Patient reported symptomatic improvement during drainage.

Specimens:
Pleural fluid sent for cell count, chemistry, culture, and cytology.

Complications:
None immediate.

Plan:
Post-procedure chest x-ray. Resume diet. Follow pleural studies.

Robotic bronchoscopy with PEF ablation.

Indication:
Biopsy-proven peripheral adenocarcinoma in the left lower lobe, treatment session.

Robotic bronchoscopy performed to a left lower lobe lesion using ION platform. Cone-beam CT used for confirmation of catheter position within the target. No central endobronchial lesion. Stable target access achieved. No major bleeding.

Specimens:
None, diagnosis previously established.

Complications:

NOTE: note_046

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_<<<NOTE _TAGS: extreme_length, reordered_sections, conflicting_details

PLAN
Admit to monitored bed, serial chest radiographs, and bronchodilator therapy.

PROCEDURE
Robotic bronchoscopy on Monarch platform to right upper lobe lesion with radial EBUS, fluoroscopy, cone-beam CT, transbronchial needle aspiration, forceps biopsy, cryobiopsy, fiducial placement, and EBUS staging.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
RUL lesion with mediastinal adenopathy; diagnosis and staging completed.

INDICATION
Enlarging right upper lobe lesion with PET-avid 4R node.

FINDINGS
No central endobronchial tumor. Robotic scope articulation allowed access to the posterior segment target. Radial EBUS showed an eccentric lesion view that became near concentric after slight repositioning. Cone-beam CT confirmed the biopsy tool within the lesion. Three fiducials were deployed after tissue acquisition. Linear EBUS identified enlarged 4R and 7 nodes. One line in the auto-import states LUL lesion, but the intended and repeatedly documented target throughout the note is RUL.

DETAILS
After airway inspection, robotic bronchoscopy was used to access the lesion. Samples obtained included TBNA x4, forceps biopsy x6, and cryobiopsy x2. Minor bleeding after cryobiopsy resolved with tamponade and suction. EBUS-TBNA then performed at 4R x5 and 7 x3. ROSE from peripheral and nodal samples suggested adequacy.

SPECIMENS
RUL lesion aspirates, forceps biopsies, cryobiopsies
4R and 7 nodal aspirates

COMPLICATIONS
Minor bleeding controlled bronchoscopically; no immediate pneumothorax.

<<<END NOTE>>>

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia.

FINDINGS

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL

Sequential valve deployment was performed to occlude the target lobe. Final inspection demonstrated satisfactory valve position and occlusion.

SPECIMENS
None.

EDGE_<<<NOTE _TAGS: reordered_sections, inconsistent_formatting

PLAN
Post-procedure chest radiograph. Follow BAL and TBBBx pathology/culture results. Discharge from bronchoscopy recovery if stable on room air.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
RUL peripheral opacity; mediastinal adenopathy.

PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Abnormal chest CT with persistent cough and PET-avid RUL lesion.

PROCEDURES PERFORMED
Flexible bronchoscopy with airway inspection
BAL, right upper lobe
Transbronchial biopsy, right upper lobe
Linear EBUS-TBNA stations 4R and 7

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia with LMA.

FINDINGS
Trachea midline. Main carina sharp. No endobronchial tumor seen. Mild friable mucosa in the anterior segment of the RUL. Station 4R enlarged and hypoechoic. Station 7 mildly enlarged.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
After timeout and induction, flexible bronchoscope was advanced through the LMA. Complete airway inspection was performed to the segmental level. BAL was obtained from the RUL with 120 mL instilled and 42 mL returned, lightly blood-tinged. Fluoroscopically guided transbronchial biopsies were then obtained from the RUL lesion. Linear EBUS scope was introduced and nodal sampling performed in the sequence 4R then 7. Station 4R underwent 5 passes, station 7 underwent 3 passes. ROSE was available and showed lymphoid tissue at both sites.

SPECIMENS

1. RUL BAL
2. RUL transbronchial biopsy
3. EBUS-TBNA station 4R x5 passes
4. EBUS-TBNA station 7 x3 passes

COMPLICATIONS
None immediate.

IMPRESSION
Diagnostic bronchoscopy with combined parenchymal and mediastinal sampling completed without immediate complication.

Persistent RML infiltrate in immunocompromised host.

A flexible bronchoscopy was performed under moderate sedation. Vocal cords were not assessed due to transnasal route intolerance and immediate advancement through the oral bite block after conversion. Tracheobronchial tree inspected to segmental bronchi. Mild diffuse erythema without focal endobronchial lesion. BAL performed in the right middle lobe with 100 mL instilled, 36 mL returned, slightly cloudy. Cytology brushings and endobronchial biopsies were not obtained. No specimen other than BAL.

Impression:
No obstructing lesion. Diagnostic BAL completed.

Complications:
Brief cough and transient oxygen desaturation to 88%, corrected with increased supplemental oxygen.

Plan:
Send BAL for bacterial, fungal, AFB, viral, and cytology studies. Discharge from procedure unit when back to baseline.

<<<END NOTE>>>

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Peripheral left lower lobe lesion.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same, status post robotic bronchoscopy on Monarch platform with radial EBUS and transbronchial sampling.

PROCEDURES PERFORMED
Robotic bronchoscopy platform navigation
Radial EBUS
Fluoroscopy
TBNA
Forceps biopsy
BAL

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia.

FINDINGS
Monarch robotic bronchoscopy platform used to reach a left lower lobe posterior basal target. Outer sheath and inner scope positioning allowed stable access. Radial EBUS demonstrated an eccentric view. Airways otherwise without endobronchial abnormality.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
After planning and bronchoscopy inspection, the robotic scope was navigated to the lesion. Sampling included TBNA x4 and forceps biopsy x7 under fluoroscopic guidance. BAL performed in the left lower lobe after tissue sampling. Hemostasis was adequate.

SPECIMENS
LLL lesion TBNA
LLL forceps biopsies
LLL BAL

COMPLICATIONS
None immediate.

PLAN
Chest radiograph in PACU. Follow pathology and microbiology results.

NOTE: note_047
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Loculated left empyema with incomplete drainage from existing pigtail catheter.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same.

PROCEDURE
Pleural ultrasound and fibrinolytic instillation through existing tube.

FINDINGS
Residual loculated left basilar collection with internal septations. Existing catheter remained intrapleural and patent after saline flush.

DETAILS
After confirming tube patency, alteplase and DNase were instilled via the left pleural catheter. Tube was clamped for dwell period. Patient had mild transient chest discomfort but remained stable.

SPECIMENS
None.

COMPLICATIONS
No immediate bleeding or respiratory decompensation.

PLAN
Return tube to suction after dwell. Repeat imaging and monitor drainage.

EDGE_<<<NOTE _TAGS: conflicting_details

PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Right mainstem stent migration.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Right mainstem stent migration, revised.

PROCEDURE
Flexible bronchoscopy with stent repositioning and secretion clearance.

FINDINGS
A silicone stent was seen partially prolapsed proximally into the distal trachea. Later in the note the stent is described as covered metallic; the intended device was the previously placed silicone right mainstem stent. Moderate secretions distal to the stent were suctioned. After repositioning, the stent sat appropriately within the right mainstem with good opening of the bronchus intermedius.

DETAILS
Under general anesthesia, rigid intervention was not required. Using forceps through flexible bronchoscopy, the migrated stent was repositioned distally. Final inspection showed good apposition and no major granulation tissue.

SPECIMENS
None.

COMPLICATIONS
None.

PLAN
Repeat surveillance bronchoscopy if symptoms recur.

Right middle lobe peripheral lesion, previously diagnosed, planned bronchoscopic cryoablation.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same, status post cryoablation.

Navigational bronchoscopy with Galaxy-assisted guidance
Cone-beam CT confirmation
Cryoablation of peripheral lesion
Track ablation

================================================================================
NOTE: note_019
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Indication:
Need for diagnosis of right middle lobe nodule and staging of mediastinum.

Procedure:
Electromagnetic navigational bronchoscopy (SuperD platform), radial EBUS, fluoroscopy, TBNA and forceps biopsy of RML target, followed by EBUS-TBNA 4R/7/11R.

Findings:
CT-planned route used to RML lesion. Registration completed without difficulty. Locatable guide advanced through extended working channel to target. Radial EBUS provided eccentric lesion view. Fluoroscopy used during sampling. No endobronchial lesion. Nodes 4R and 11R enlarged.

Sampling:
RML TBNA x3
RML forceps x6
4R x5 passes
7 x3 passes
11R x4 passes

ROSE:
Available from the peripheral lesion and 4R, showing lesional cells in target and adequate nodal sampling.

Complications:
None immediate.

Plan:
Chest x-ray after procedure and follow final pathology.

NOTE: note_022

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Procedure note:
Linear EBUS with EUS-B added for inaccessible station.

Indication:
Need for mediastinal staging of left hilar mass.

Findings:
Stations 11L, 7, and 4L were sampled bronchoscopically. EUS-B was then used to sample station 8 because of favorable esophageal window. Limited airway exam showed extrinsic compression of the left upper lobe bronchus without endobronchial lesion.

Sampling order:
11L x4 passes
7 x4 passes
4L x5 passes
8 via EUS-B x3 passes

ROSE:
Adequate lymphoid tissue from all stations; atypical cells noted from 4L.

Complications:
None immediate.

Plan:
Await final cytology. Resume diet after recovery.

<<<END NOTE>>>

Procedure note: bronchoscopy through tracheostomy.

Indication: mucus plugging and increased airway pressures.
A bronchoscope was passed through the mature tracheostomy tube. Thick tenacious secretions were occluding the distal tube and proximal left mainstem; these were suctioned clear. Distal tip of the tube sat 3 cm above the carina. No specimen obtained.
Tolerated well without desaturation. Continue humidification and routine trach care.

EDGE_<<<NOTE _TAGS: missing_section, copy_paste_artifacts

PROCEDURE: Mature trach exchange + bronchoscopy through trach

INDICATION:
Difficulty passing suction catheter and cuff leak. Difficulty passing suction catheter and cuff leak.

FINDINGS:
Existing tracheostomy tube partially obstructed by dried secretions. Mature tract present. Distal trachea and main carina visualized. New tube tip approximately 2.5 cm above carina. Mild tracheal irritation, no false passage.

DETAILS:
The existing cuffed tube was removed over a bougie and replaced with a new cuffed tracheostomy tube of the same size. Flexible bronchoscope was advanced through the new tube to confirm intratracheal position and evaluate the distal airway. Secretions were suctioned from the lower trachea and right mainstem.

SPECIMENS:
None.

COMPLICATIONS:
None immediate.

PLAN:
Routine trach care, humidification, monitor cuff pressures.

<<<END NOTE>>>

Procedure:
Bronchoscopic ablation of peripheral pulmonary lesion.

Indication:
Growing peripheral pulmonary nodule in a poor surgical candidate.

Findings:
Lesion located in the right lower lobe by pre-procedure imaging. Navigation and imaging confirmation were used. Immediate post-treatment inspection showed no active airway bleeding. One key truth state, specifically exact lesion size, is not documented anywhere in this note.

Technique:
After guided bronchoscopy to the target, ablation catheter was positioned and treatment delivered. Cone-beam CT confirmed target engagement before ablation and post-ablation changes afterward. Track ablation was performed during device withdrawal.

Ablation modality:
Microwave ablation.

Specimens:
None obtained in this session.

Complications:
No immediate pneumothorax or major bleeding.

Plan:
Post-procedure chest radiograph and observation.

================================================================================
NOTE: note_016
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Right lower lobe cavitary lesion.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same.

PROCEDURES
Flexible bronchoscopy with BAL, protected brushings, endobronchial biopsy, and transbronchial biopsy.

INDICATION
Hemoptysis and persistent cavitary RLL abnormality.

FINDINGS
Mild mucosal edema and hyperemia in the bronchus intermedius and basilar segmental bronchi. No frank endobronchial mass. Purulent secretions noted from the superior segment of the right lower lobe.

DESCRIPTION
Complete airway inspection performed. BAL obtained from the superior segment of the RLL with 140 mL instilled and 50 mL returned. Protected brushings obtained from the same subsegment. Subtle friable mucosa at the segmental takeoff underwent endobronchial biopsy. Fluoroscopically guided transbronchial biopsies were also obtained.

SPECIMENS
RLL BAL
RLL brushings
Endobronchial biopsy, RLL
Transbronchial biopsies, RLL

COMPLICATIONS
Small self-limited bleed after transbronchial biopsy, controlled with wedging and suction.

PLAN
Follow pathology and cultures. Chest radiograph post-procedure.

<<<END NOTE>>>

EDGE_<<<NOTE _TAGS: copy_paste_artifacts, inconsistent_formatting

PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Mucus plugging, right lower lobe atelectasis

PROCEDURE
Flexible bronchoscopy with therapeutic aspiration and BAL BAL

Findings
Copious thick secretions in bronchus intermedius and right lower lobe basilar segments. Underlying mucosa mildly erythematous. No endobronchial mass.

Details
Bronchoscope advanced through ETT. Repeated suctioning and saline lavage used to clear plugging. After therapeutic clearance, BAL was obtained from the right lower lobe for culture because of concern for pneumonia.

Specimens
RLL BAL.

Complications
Transient bronchospasm responded to bronchodilator therapy.

Plan
Continue pulmonary hygiene, antibiotics per primary team, follow BAL.

STATUS: SUCCESS

================================================================================
NOTE: note_028
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Endobronchial tumor causing right upper lobe collapse.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same, status post tumor debulking and APC.

PROCEDURES
Flexible bronchoscopy
Mechanical debulking
APC

FINDINGS
Tumor arising from the right upper lobe bronchus extended to the distal right mainstem with near-complete occlusion of the RUL orifice. Bronchus intermedius remained patent. After debulking and APC, the RUL takeoff was partially recanalized though distal segmental patency remained limited by tumor.

DETAILS
Under general anesthesia, forceps debulking was used to remove friable tumor from the right upper lobe bronchus. APC was applied for tumor devitalization and hemostasis. Large clot and debris were suctioned clear.

SPECIMENS
Endobronchial tumor tissue.

COMPLICATIONS
Minor bleeding controlled with APC and iced saline.

PLAN
Chest radiograph. Oncology and radiation oncology follow-up per inpatient team.

<<<END NOTE>>>

NOTE: note_031

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Need for mediastinal staging in suspected lung cancer.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same.

PROCEDURE
Linear EBUS-TBNA with elastography.

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia.

FINDINGS
Limited airway survey without endobronchial lesion. Elastography used selectively; station 4R appeared relatively stiff and was prioritized. Stations sampled included 4R, 7, and 11R. Doppler confirmed avascular window before each pass.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
EBUS bronchoscope advanced and systematic nodal survey performed. Sampling order was 11R, 4R, then 7. Passes: 11R x3, 4R x5, 7 x4. ROSE was not available.

SPECIMENS
EBUS-TBNA 11R, 4R, 7.

COMPLICATIONS
None immediate.

PLAN
Await final cytology. Recovery per anesthesia.

<<<END NOTE>>>

================================================================================
NOTE: note_018
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Narrative op note

A therapeutic flexible bronchoscopy was performed for mucus plugging and left lower lobe atelectasis. Under general anesthesia via endotracheal tube, the bronchoscope was advanced and found copious thick yellow-white secretions filling the left mainstem and left lower lobe bronchi. Therapeutic aspiration was performed with repeated saline aliquots and suctioning until the left-sided airways were patent. Mild underlying bronchomalacia of the left lower lobe bronchi was present. No tumor or foreign body identified. No specimen was sent because the purpose of the procedure was clearance rather than diagnosis. The patient tolerated the procedure well. Post-procedure plan is continued aggressive pulmonary hygiene and ventilator weaning as able.

<<<END NOTE>>>

================================================================================
NOTE: note_026
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Procedure:
Diagnostic bronchoscopy with BAL and brushings.

Indication:
Persistent right upper lobe tree-in-bud opacities and chronic cough.

Technique:
Flexible bronchoscopy under moderate sedation. Airways examined to subsegmental level. BAL from posterior segment of the RUL with 90 mL instilled and 28 mL returned. Cytology brushings obtained from the same segment.

Findings:
Diffuse mild mucosal friability and scant mucoid secretions in the RUL. No mass, foreign body, or significant stenosis.

Specimens:
RUL BAL, RUL brushings.

Complications:
None immediate.

Plan:
Send BAL for bacterial, fungal, AFB, and cytology studies.

================================================================================
NOTE: note_013
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Indication:
Recurrent left pleural effusion and pleural nodularity on CT.

Procedure:
Medical pleuroscopy with pleural biopsies and talc pleurodesis.

Consent:
Obtained.

Technique:
Under monitored anesthesia care, patient positioned right lateral decubitus. Ultrasound confirmed moderate left pleural effusion. Entry made in the left midaxillary line and pleural space accessed. Pleuroscope introduced after drainage of serosanguinous fluid.

Findings:
Multiple pleural nodules and diffuse pleural studding over parietal pleura and diaphragm. No frank empyema. Lung partially expandable. Approximately 1.1 L fluid drained.

Specimens:
Multiple parietal pleural biopsies submitted to pathology. Pleural fluid sent for cytology.

Additional intervention:
Sterile talc poudrage performed at conclusion of <<<NOTE .

Complications:
None immediate.

Plan:
Chest tube to suction overnight. Daily chest radiograph. Follow pathology/cytology.

<<<END NOTE>>>

================================================================================
NOTE: note_005
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Indication:
PET-avid left lower lobe nodule with hilar uptake.

Procedure:
Robotic bronchoscopy using shape-sensing navigation platform (ION), radial EBUS confirmation, fluoroscopy, cone-beam CT spin, transbronchial needle aspiration, forceps biopsy, cryobiopsy, and BAL. Linear EBUS-TBNA of 11L and 7.

Consent:
Informed consent obtained.

Technique:
Following CT-based pathway planning, robotic bronchoscopy was performed to a peripheral LLL target. Stable catheter position at the lesion was achieved. Radial EBUS showed a concentric view. Cone-beam CT confirmed tool-in-lesion. Multiple samples obtained by 21G needle, forceps, and 1.1 mm cryoprobe. BAL was performed in the same segment. Linear EBUS was then performed for nodal staging.

Findings:
LLL peripheral lesion measured approximately 2.3 cm by pre-procedure imaging. No endobronchial lesion. Station 11L enlarged; station 7 borderline. ROSE from the peripheral target showed lesional material. Elastography not used.

Sampling:
Peripheral lesion: TBNA x4, forceps x6, cryobiopsy x2
11L: 4 passes
7: 3 passes

Specimens:
Peripheral lesion aspirates, forceps tissue, cryobiopsy tissue, LLL BAL, EBUS-TBNA 11L and 7.

Complications:
Trace bleeding after cryobiopsy controlled with wedging and suction. No immediate pneumothorax.

Plan:
Portable chest x-ray in recovery. Await pathology and cytology.

<<<END NOTE>>>

================================================================================
NOTE: note_004
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PRE-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Malignant central airway obstruction involving the distal trachea and right mainstem bronchus.

POST-PROCEDURE DIAGNOSIS
Same, status post rigid bronchoscopy with tumor debulking and stent placement.

PROCEDURES PERFORMED
Rigid bronchoscopy
Mechanical tumor debulking
APC ablation
Balloon dilation of right mainstem bronchus
Airway stent placement

ANESTHESIA
General anesthesia with jet ventilation.

FINDINGS
Exophytic friable tumor involved the distal trachea and extended into the proximal right mainstem bronchus causing approximately 80% luminal obstruction. Distal right bronchial tree visible after debulking with patent bronchus intermedius. Left mainstem bronchus patent.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL
Rigid bronchoscope was introduced after induction. Mechanical coring and forceps debulking were performed to reduce intraluminal tumor burden. APC was applied to residual bleeding tumor surfaces. A CRE balloon was used to dilate the right mainstem to 10 mm. Given persistent extrinsic compression and residual narrowing, a covered self-expanding metallic airway stent was deployed across the distal trachea into the right mainstem with satisfactory position under bronchoscopic visualization. Final inspection showed marked improvement in lumen caliber and hemostasis.

SPECIMENS
Endobronchial tumor debris/tissue sent to pathology.

COMPLICATIONS
Minor oozing controlled endoscopically.

IMPRESSION
Severe malignant central airway obstruction successfully palliated with multimodality therapy and stent placement.

PLAN
Nebulized saline, aggressive pulmonary toilet, chest radiograph, and surveillance bronchoscopy as indicated.

<<<END NOTE>>>

STATUS: SUCCESS

================================================================================
NOTE: note_042
================================================================================

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Procedure:
Linear EBUS-TBNA and endobronchial biopsy.

Indication:
Left hilar fullness with mild hemoptysis.

Findings:
A friable endobronchial lesion partially narrowed the lingular bronchus. Enlarged nodes at station 7 and 11L.

Technique:
Flexible bronchoscopy first identified the lingular lesion, which underwent forceps endobronchial biopsy. Linear EBUS then performed. Station 11L sampled x4 passes and station 7 x4 passes. ROSE showed lesional cells from the endobronchial lesion and adequate lymphoid tissue from both nodes.

Specimens:
Lingular endobronchial biopsy, EBUS-TBNA 11L and 7.

Complications:
Minimal bleeding from endobronchial biopsy controlled with topical epinephrine.

Plan:
Await pathology and cytology. Recovery uneventful.

<<<END NOTE>>>
